  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a030741-db5c-4521-8258-6d6554ac5935'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13881911431961532283">The formerly glorious god Apollo, cast down to earth in punishment by Zeus, is now an awkward mortal teenager named Lester Papadopoulos. In order to regain his place on Mount Olympus, Lester must restore five Oracles that have gone dark. But he has to achieve this impossible task without having any godly powers and while being duty-bound to a confounding young daughter of </span>
  <span id="freeText13881911431961532283" style="display:none">The formerly glorious god Apollo, cast down to earth in punishment by Zeus, is now an awkward mortal teenager named Lester Papadopoulos. In order to regain his place on Mount Olympus, Lester must restore five Oracles that have gone dark. But he has to achieve this impossible task without having any godly powers and while being duty-bound to a confounding young daughter of Demeter named Meg. <i>Thanks a lot, Dad.</i><br /><br />With the help of some demigod friends, Lester managed to survive his first two trials, one at Camp Half-Blood, and one in Indianapolis, where Meg received the Dark Prophecy. The words she uttered while seated on the Throne of Memory revealed that an evil triumvirate of Roman emperors plans to attack Camp Jupiter. While Leo flies ahead on Festus to warn the Roman camp, Lester and Meg must go through the Labyrinth to find the third emperor—and an Oracle who speaks in word puzzles—somewhere in the American Southwest. There is one glimmer of hope in the gloom-filled prophecy: <i>The cloven guide alone the way does know</i>. They will have a satyr companion, and Meg knows just who to call upon. . . .</span>
  <a data-text-id="13881911431961532283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I've shipped them since Apollo's series was announced. I'm crossing my fingers that Apollo meets her in this book since he and Meg are on their way to<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I've shipped them since Apollo's series was announced. I'm crossing my fingers that Apollo meets her in this book since he and Meg are on their way to Camp Jupiter. But it will most likely take them until the last twenty or so pages of the book to get there. So they probably won't interact much until the next book. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

</div>

<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1129400'><a id="like_count_community_question_1129400" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1129400?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">4 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28006096-the-burning-maze">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/22042228-valentina-markasovi"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1462127422i/22042228._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/22042228-valentina-markasovi">Valentina Markasović</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Since Nero referred to him as his 'kinsman', and assuming that means another emperor of the Julio-Claudian dynasty, I'd say it's going to be Caligula.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Since Nero referred to him as his 'kinsman', and assuming that means another emperor of the Julio-Claudian dynasty, I'd say it's going to be Caligula. We'll see if my guess was right!<br /><br />EDIT: Having just finished the book, I've got another hint. The prophecy's <i>master of the swift white horse</i> might refer to Caligula making his beloved horse a consul (was that horse even swift, or white? Only time will tell.). The <i>in thine own enemy's boots</i> part might be a a play on Caligula's nickname (little boot). Still, I'm sure that R. Riordan will manage to surprise us with his interpretation of the prophecy! <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=favorites-2018">favorites-2018</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997341522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15090670435729140566"><b>
  <blockquote>“Pain is an interesting thing. You think you have reached your limit and you can’t possibly feel more tortured. Then you discover there is still another level of agony. And another level after that.” </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527527310i/25610409._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Dear Mr.Riordan, <br/>The Burning Maze wasn’t what I expected at all. You dared to DO THAT in this book, and yes, I’m here weeping for what you’ve done. The book is like the mixture of The Battle of the Labyrinth and The House of Hades which turns up to be my favorite of the year since I was halfway </span>
  <span id="freeText15090670435729140566" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“Pain is an interesting thing. You think you have reached your limit and you can’t possibly feel more tortured. Then you discover there is still another level of agony. And another level after that.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1527527310i/25610409._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dear Mr.Riordan, <br>The Burning Maze wasn’t what I expected at all. You dared to DO THAT in this book, and yes, I’m here weeping for what you’ve done. The book is like the mixture of The Battle of the Labyrinth and The House of Hades which turns up to be my favorite of the year since I was halfway through it. There's no moment when I got bored or annoyed by the characters, not at all.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Satyrs aren't dryads, but we have roots, too. Camp Half Blood is mine.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>To be honest, Lester isn't always my favorite character when I started reading the first book. He's immature and often gets everyone in trouble. He is indeed Apollo but actually he doesn't act like one. Besides, Meg is also a dull character that I almost look over her all the time. Yet they're the reasons why I'm in love with this book so much that I can't get my mind back to normal even though I finished it like two weeks ago.<br><br>The book starts off with the gang exploring the maze while they're being chased by the avian creatures (i forget what they're called. so please forgive me lol). After they survive, Lester must to seek the third oracle whom he sees in his dream that she's the one being captured and used to lure him to the trap. However, he's left with no choices. Apollo must cooperate with Jason and Piper in order to acheive what he's set out to do.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527527310ra/25610410.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There're so many twists and turns in this book and I dare say it's a real tearjerking and groundbreaking book that got me crazy with I finished. The cadence is very perfect and made me laugh so many times. The best of all is the development of the main characters after what they have been through making me so pround.<br><br>And the ending tore me apart. So be prepared!<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Remember what it's like to be human,” </blockquote>
</b></span>

<div id="review_2001377904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001377904" />
    <a title="Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor"><img alt="Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542815566p2/52489703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2001377904?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor">Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=mythology-books">mythology-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001377904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16286048265156639728"><i>"It's been my observation," I said, "that you humans are more than the sum of your history. You can choose how much of your ancestry to embrace. You can overcome the expectations of your family and your society. What you cannot do, and should never do, is try to be someone other than yourself."</i><br/><br/>...<br/><br/>*screams into the void*<br/><br/>Whelp. Rick's done it. <b>Not since <i>The Mark of Athena</i> have I felt so destroyed by a Rick Riordan book.</b><br/><br/>IT'S NOT FAIR I TELL YOU.<br/><br/>*swings back wine bottle*<br/><br/>Okay. I think I'm ready to ta</span>
  <span id="freeText16286048265156639728" style="display:none"><i>"It's been my observation," I said, "that you humans are more than the sum of your history. You can choose how much of your ancestry to embrace. You can overcome the expectations of your family and your society. What you cannot do, and should never do, is try to be someone other than yourself."</i><br /><br />...<br /><br />*screams into the void*<br /><br />Whelp. Rick's done it. <b>Not since <i>The Mark of Athena</i> have I felt so destroyed by a Rick Riordan book.</b><br /><br />IT'S NOT FAIR I TELL YOU.<br /><br />*swings back wine bottle*<br /><br />Okay. I think I'm ready to talk about this.<br /><br /><i>The Burning Maze</i> is the third book in The Trials of Apollo series, and Rick Riordan's <b>nineteenth</b> demigod book. I've read every single one of this man's books, and I'm never disappointed. So it shouldn't be a surprise that I absolutely <b>loved</b> this.<br /><br />I sound like a broken record at this point, but I don't care. This series is just...so special. I love all of Rick's books, sure, but there's something about The Trials of Apollo that just <b>
  <i>gets me.</i>
</b> This series centers around Apollo, the shining Greek god of archery, music, medicine, and the Sun, among other things. At the beginning of the first book, Zeus casts Apollo out of Olympus as punishment for his failures, and traps him in the body of a 16 year old boy named Lester Papadopoulos. Cursed with mortality, acne, and flab, Apollo must complete five trials in order to restore himself to his godly glory.<br /><br />Apollo is still one of the funniest Rick Riordan characters ever put on the page. <b>His voice is biting, self-absorbed, and utterly hysterical.</b> He's not your conventional hero. He's not selfless, or brave, and he has absolutely <i>no qualms</i> about it. And that's what makes him great.<br /><br />But, Apollo has gone through a lot since the beginning of the first book, and he has much more to lose.<br /><br />What surprised me most about Apollo's character is how much growth he's experienced since book one. Our main character has lived for millennia, and he carries quite a bit of baggage from his past. On top of his past failures, Apollo is consistently confronted by his own mortality, and becomes all too familiar with the pain and love that comes with being human. Seeing his growth has been so powerful, and incredibly emotional.<br /><br />The relationships he forms in this series are also <b>wonderful</b>. I'll continue to harp on the fact that <b>Meg and Apollo have the most adorable friendship <i>ever.</i></b> Yeah, you heard me. Who knew the friendship between a former all-powerful god and a twelve-year-old girl would be so goddamn <b>beautiful?</b> <br /><br />Our cast of side characters bring a ton to the story as well. I loved seeing more of the nymphs and dryads in this installment, and there were some <i>amazing</i> cameos in here. <b>I've missed Grover so much.</b> What a delight he was! Coach Hedge, Piper, and Jason were also welcome additions to this cast of characters.<br /><br /><b>I LOVE EVERYONE.</b><br /><br />*breathes*<br /><br />Sorry.<br /><br />On top of all that, <i>The Burning Maze</i> has the best villain this series has seen so far. I won't name the crazy Roman Emperor that makes an appearance in this installment, but he was...<b>disgustingly evil.</b> Quite the fitting villain, and a terrifying foil for our characters.<br /><br />The story constantly kept me on my toes, and this was definitely a lot darker than the previous two books in the series. There was this feeling of constant <i>dread</i> interwoven throughout the narrative. The emotion was heightened to astronomical proportions, and <b>I freaking cried my eyes out at one point.</b> Sobbed. <br /><br />The Trials of Apollo is an all-time-favorite for a reason, guys. <b>It's that good.</b><br /><br />With just the right balance of laughs and emotion, wonderful characters, a batshit crazy villain, and an exciting story set in the depths of the Labyrinth, <i>The Burning Maze</i> succeeds on so many levels. I absolutely <b>adored</b> this book. How, oh <i>how</i> will I wait for the fourth book?What must I do to get my hands on it?!<br /><br />The wait might just kill me, but <b>I'm so ready.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16286048265156639728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15044723030988451595" style="display:none"><b>Complete 5 Golden Stars</b><br />&amp; 5 thousands plus!<br /><br />the Hidden Oracle: ★★★★★/5= 5: Marvelous<br />the Dark Prophecy: ★★★★★/5= 4.75: Gorgeous<br />the Burning Maze: ★★★★★/5= 5 Compelete!!!: Supercalifragilisticexpialidocious! Marvelous! Gorgeous! Incredible! Unbelievable!....Legendary!......<br /><br />I,<br />Daughter of Apollo,<br />from Camp Half-Blood,<br />a Healer from Cabin 7,<br />announce this book<br />As<br /><i>*dramatic pause*</i><br /><br /><i><b>PERFECTION!</b>!</i><br /><br />One word,<br /><i>says it all!</i><br />In my point of view, one of the features of a perfect book is when you wish a thing to take place (which made you squeal fangirling, anticipation, not prediction), it actually happens. Not to mention, I wished sooooooooo many things during this book &amp; all came true!<br /><i>I'm thrilled! I'm blessed! I'm fangirling!</i><br />Rick Riordan knows how to build up an <b>anticipation</b> when it is its time &amp; in the best thrilling funniest possible way!!<br />I loved it, page by page, wholeheartedly! &lt;3 every second of reading it, every word, swallowed me up!<br />~book 3 of every series Rick Riordan wrote (so far) is where the story started to ascend higher with steep slope! You just should wait until book 3 then BOOM! more thrilling! more mysteries! more revealing! etc. book 1 &amp; 2 are fabulous too but they are more like an introduction, the basis of the story to be build up on them.~<br /><br />I can see how it will go on! No. Not really, I can't predict anything. I just know it gonna BLOW UP!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Rick Riordan is beyond Genius!</b>
</i><br /><br />He can create such <b>intense</b> moments in which my heart was racing over 120 &amp; it lasted for more than 50 pages constantly! (I LOVE THAT FEELING!) also there was intense plus fun at some points!<br />Same happening for <b>laughter</b>! Usually, I burst into laughter for 30 minutes straight! &amp; my parents were like <i>"what's happening? you're just reading a book!"</i>. &amp; my throat hurt after that but it was worth it! I still laughs by just remembering them!<br />Riordan’s jokes never gets old. &amp; they are PRICELESS!<br /><br /><i>Apollo himself! (he ascended to my top 4 truly favourite characters! not just because his jokes, explaining later)<br />Apollo's Narration!<br />all Apollo's comments &amp; thoughts!<br />all the readers’ comments!<br />Chapters haikus!<br />Meg!<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Grover! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />the Arrow of Dodona!<br />the crossword puzzles!</i><br />I can't remember more to mention but there is definitely more. XD<br />you can see some more in my quotes below. (if you read the book, that might have spoilers too.)<br /><br />Many words of <b>wisdom</b>! Inspiring Apollo &amp; others! (I love to see hopeful quotes in my favourite books, they made me keep going on the hard times.)<br /><br /><i>“It’s been my observation" I said, “that you humans are more than the sum of your history. You can choose how much of your ancestry to embrace. You can overcome the expectations of your family and your society. What you cannot do, and should never do, is try to be someone other than yourself"</i><br /><br />&amp; all the <b>Characters</b> (in the whole Half-blood chronicles) are awesome. Villains too are interesting; cruel &amp; sometimes even fun!<br />In all Riordan's books, I love the villains too; from Kronos, Titans &amp; Gaea to Triumvirate. my favourites in special: Lit, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Medea, Pandai, Blemmyae, Caligula <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> &amp; I'm the one from good guys side (loving the heroes) who said that. &amp; that says something! like how perfect the characters are build up!<br />also <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I started to like Piper. (tho I hated her too at some points.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><b>THIS BOOK WAS EXTRAORDINARY AMAZING!</b><br /><br />and covered my <i>
  <b>guilty pleasure</b>
</i> very very very very well! from the first!<br />in which I LOVE to see my favourite character, suffer. (or breakdown; that'll work too.)<br /><i>*evil laughter*</i><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[intense moments from the beginning!<br />He was tortured<br />He was captured<br />So many times.<br />just to clarify; I don't want them (fav characters) to die. Suffer &amp; Survive is good! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />In these cases, My internal evil maniac laughing (so did I (mostly smiling), but sometimes I forced myself not to!)<br /><br />also I love to <b>cry</b> over a book! I loved him when he was so clueless &amp; seriously being funny in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169301063" rel="nofollow noopener">the Lost Hero</a>.<br />&amp; I cried every time I remembered that or they mentioned him after that. tho I was spoiled by that, months ago, &amp; I tried to forget that but I couldn't. I was looking forward to it. &amp; thanks to blessing writing style of Riordan (I really mean it, it's not a sarcasm) it happened at the unexpectedly unexpected time &amp; I was shocked &amp; cried when it happened.<br /><br />burst out crying again at these parts during Re-Reading too ;_;<br /><br /><i>It struck me just how young he was—no more than seventeen.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />it has so much feelz here &amp; there.<br />it's ended.<br />&amp; next book coming next Fall!<br /><br />-<br />As it is my <i>First</i> Riordan's series to come up with (including being fangirl update, looking for news &amp; waiting for the books), so I wrote a Pure Emotional review over it (which I read in its publication year too) &amp; as you can see it is different; all my feelings, all my thoughts, all my fangirling have been gathered in one place &amp; I tried to show as much love as I could say in words.<br />I actually, truly love this review! &amp; proud of it! &lt;3<br />-<br />sums it up:<br />World building: ★★★★★/5<br />Characters development: ★★★★★/5<br />Written style: ★★★★★/5<br />/ Fun: ★★★★★/5<br />/ Feelz: ★★★★★/5<br />plot &amp; events: ★★★★★/5<br />General idea: ★★★★★/5<br />-<br /><b>first read: [2018: Dec 1-Dec 4]</b><br />Really glad to read this <i>Bless</i> in my birthmonth, December!<br />I tried to swallow it up! tasted every pages, every words; because first time surprise is only once!<br />&amp; I set a record!     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1990734428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1990734428" />
    <a title="- ̗̀  jess  ̖́-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7235660---jess--"><img alt="- ̗̀  jess  ̖́-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527737790p2/7235660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1990734428?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="- ̗̀  jess  ̖́-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="- ̗̀  jess  ̖́-" href="/user/show/7235660---jess--">- ̗̀  jess  ̖́-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1990734428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15724482499741579921">Hey folks! It's that time of year when I write a really incoherent screamy review about Rick Riordan's books and I get told to chill, but I have no chill when it comes to Rick Riordan. And believe me when I say that this time, Rick Riordan is <i>not</i> fucking around. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong - for a lot of the book, we've got the same fun adventure romp that many readers have come to love about Rick's books, even if it is somewhat formulaic. We've got Apollo in all his melodrama, with soooooooo many refere</span>
  <span id="freeText15724482499741579921" style="display:none">Hey folks! It's that time of year when I write a really incoherent screamy review about Rick Riordan's books and I get told to chill, but I have no chill when it comes to Rick Riordan. And believe me when I say that this time, Rick Riordan is <i>not</i> fucking around. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong - for a lot of the book, we've got the same fun adventure romp that many readers have come to love about Rick's books, even if it is somewhat formulaic. We've got Apollo in all his melodrama, with soooooooo many references to pop culture and history, for both modern teenagers AND their parents. So many. SO. MANY. Apollo, as always, is such a horrifying delight to read, because he's a disaster, and he's so conceited, but it's all very endearing. That being said, I believe that Apollo's a lot more sympathetic than he was in the first or second books - he's learned some humility. His earlier adventures have stuck with him, and it was great to see so much character development. <br /><br />It was really exciting seeing Grover again, and seeing how much he's matured. I'm so proud of him. And the Hedge family - I really grew into loving the three of them in this book, even though I didn't really pay them a lot of heed in the Heroes of Olympus. We also got some old villains, like Medea, which was really cool to see. <br /><br />Spoilers from this point on. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was so excited for Piper and Jason, because I've really come to love them, even though when I first read <i>The Lost Hero</i>, I was not a fan of any of them. I was twelve. In the eight years in between, I have come to love each and every member of the Seven, including Leo Valdez, even if he can be really annoying. Especially since reading <i>The House of Hades</i>, I've really come to realize how much I love everything about Piper and Jason - I'm not a huge Jasiper fan, but I know now I love them in <i>The Lost Hero</i>, and all the books in between. <br /><br />So the first shock of the book: Jasiper broke up. I was stunned, because this contradicted everything we had seen from the ending of the Heroes of Olympus, with everyone neatly paired off and getting a happily-ever-after. We all thought that they were going to get a happily-ever-after. But I thought that this was a really mature look on first love. While Percy and Annabeth are proof that first love can be your true love - as it was for Rick himself - Piper and Jason proves that things aren't always that cut and dry. Leo and Calypso, in <i>The Dark Prophecy</i>, talked about how they needed to find time to figure out how to be a couple away from travelling and danger. Piper and Jason figured that they weren't a good couple, but they were still friends, and that was okay. <br /><br />Even seeing both Piper and Jason was so bittersweet, and it hurt that Piper's life was turned upside down. I admire how incredibly brave she was, dealing with so much in such a short time - even before the events of this book. And when we finally see Jason, we see him just the way as he's aways been - quiet, dedicated, loyal. The same qualities that I pegged him as 'boring' when I first met him in the end made me love him. And it was good to see that Jason, at least, was living as normal of a life that demigods can. <br /><br />I have to admit that I had, up until this recent reread and this book, that I considered <i>Trials of Apollo</i> to be the most juvenile of Rick's series. But it's not: the silliness hides the brutality and tragedy that has always been inherent in Greek mythology, and, well, the Camp Half-Blood-verse as a whole. This book really brought it into the forefront. On the first page of <i>The Lightning Thief</i>, Percy says, "Being a half-blood is dangerous. It's scary. Most of the time, it gets you killed in painful, scary ways." And sure, we've seen some pretty brutal deaths over the years. But Rick doesn't kill main characters. If he does, he brings them back. Or so we thought. <br /><br />Because Jason. Jason Grace dies and even though I am in denial, it is made incredibly clear that this is final. There is no Piper charmspeaking him to life. No potion. No godly magic. We see him get stabbed, twice. We see his body. We see his coffin. In all Rick Riordan's books, this is the most final and brutal death, because it's so goddamn <i>real</i>. I think that a lot of other deaths in the series had hope and fantasy behind them: Beckendorf and Silena reunited in Elysium, Zoe Nightshade turning into a constellation, Bianca di Angelo showing up in ghost form - and even so, these were minor characters. They were sad, but you only knew them for a book or so. You don't spend FIVE FUCKING BOOKS with them only to see them end up in a coffin. <br /><br />Jason's death is one of the hardest depictions of loss I've ever seen in a book, because it's so frank and human. It takes on a view of death that I've seen in books for older readers. I think it was very reminiscent of One Particular Death in one of Leigh Bardugo's books. He doesn't get a romantic monologue of dying like Luke or Silena did. It was quick and brutal. And realizing it was just as - Jason's corpse tumbling onto the beach. Even though he finished his Grand Quest, he wasn't safe, because <i>demigods aren't safe</i> - and neither are humans, for that matter. It's a very straightforward look at mortality. Sometimes people die gracelessly (I'M SORRY, I'M SO FUCKING SORRY). Sometimes people die too early. Sometimes people die when no one expected them to. I have criticized Rick for not killing anyone in his books, that this lowers the stakes. I think we all didn't expect the stakes to be raised so quickly. Like Caligula says: it's not a game. And this book shows it. <br /><br />I also have to commend Rick for this depiction of grief, because it's so fucking raw. Jason's death didn't really hit me until Leo flew in and asked, "Where's Jason," and I <i>screamed</i> because I realized Jason and Leo never got to say goodbye to each other. Hell, Jason never knew that Leo was ALIVE. Like, excuse me, I'm going to go cry under a rock now. Not to mention Leo going, "I can't even think right now? Is that normal? Just forgetting how to think?" That also hit me so hard because it was so real and human. And I think, if this book had been out when my dad passed away, this would have been the book I'd turn to for solace, because it covers all these complex and hard feelings about death and loss that you don't fully realize until someone you care about dies. Apollo found those feelings. <br /><br />Jason Grace died as he lived, for the most part: selflessly and heroically (though, notably, it wasn't a brick that killed him). And even though his death fucking hurts, I think it's given everyone a lot more fire to defeat the emperors. I have a lot of complicated feelings right now, because I only just finished the book and this is the worst fictional death I've gone through, like, ever. But I really do commend Rick Riordan on how he handled everything, even if I'm going to be shrieking into the next century. <br /><br />As for the end: Bellona's daughter. On the one hand, this means we'll see Reyna again, one of my favourite characters. On the other, I don't believe we got Leo's bad news from Camp Jupiter? Also, I'm really really really really not wanting this Reyna/Apollo thing to happen, so I have a lot of mixed feelings? I just. Have. A lot of feelings about this book. I have no chill. I'm sorry. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So to sum it all up, in one non-spoilery sentence: Rick Riordan does it again - a fun adventurous romp through mythology, history, Roman emperors, and a bit of emotional turmoil thrown in, just for funsies. I'm really anticipating the next book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15724482499741579921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1992878125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8770837062207563705"><i>Thank you Penguin Random House for a full copy. All thoughts are my own</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.ambsreads.wordpress.com/2018/04/17/the-burning-maze-by-rick-riordan-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YOU CAN ALSO FIND MY REVIEWS FOR ALL THE BOOKS IN THIS SERIES ON MY BLOG! CLICK HERE</a><br/><br/>Dare I say it? I may just. The Burning Maze is one of Rick Riordan’s top five books of all time. This book had it all. Character development that didn’t fade away, action, death, drama and the inclusion of past characters didn’t feel forced. Oh, I forgot to mention the best part! The Burning Maze brought back Grover. I honestly feel as if Grov</span>
  <span id="freeText8770837062207563705" style="display:none"><i>Thank you Penguin Random House for a full copy. All thoughts are my own</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.ambsreads.wordpress.com/2018/04/17/the-burning-maze-by-rick-riordan-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">YOU CAN ALSO FIND MY REVIEWS FOR ALL THE BOOKS IN THIS SERIES ON MY BLOG! CLICK HERE</a><br /><br />Dare I say it? I may just. The Burning Maze is one of Rick Riordan’s top five books of all time. This book had it all. Character development that didn’t fade away, action, death, drama and the inclusion of past characters didn’t feel forced. Oh, I forgot to mention the best part! The Burning Maze brought back Grover. I honestly feel as if Grover is one of the most underappreciated characters in all of Rick Riordan’s series. That satyr deserves a heck of a lot more recognition for what he’s gone through and the fact he was here in The Burning Maze? You bet I screamed.<br /><br />The Burning Maze kicks off almost hours after the end of The Dark Prophecy. Meg, Apollo and Grover are travelling through the labyrinth (yes, the labyrinth is back) and are facing some complications, obviously. The trio goes through so much and at times even has to spilt up. However, I notice Rick Riordan always makes sure to use the Camp Half-Blood rule of three people going on a quest together. In The Burning Maze, we learn more about Meg’s biological father and see her interact with dryads of where she used to live. Piper and Jason even appear, characters from one of Rick Riordan’s other series, and they didn’t make me want to die (these two were my least favourite of Rick Riordan’s).<br /><br />This story just seems to flow so much better than the previous one. It was honestly so exciting and I am so happy that I can passionately tell everyone to pick it up. If you’re into middle grade and Rick Riordan’s books this is so worth it.<br /><br />Rick really changed up the game in this one is all I’ll say without spoiling anyone. I’m just so excited for people to read it so I have people to scream with.<br /><br />Anyway, I’m babbling, let us jump into what I liked and didn’t like about The Burning Maze.<br /><br />L I K E S<br />✗ RICK CHANGED IT UP IM THRIVING<br /><br />It’s not that Rick changed it up, it’s that he finally did things he was too afraid to do in previous books. I really can’t say much here without spoiling it and I want everyone to be as shocked as I was, so I’ll leave it at that.<br /><br />✗ I ACTUALLY ENJOYED JASON AND PIPER I AM SHOOKETH<br /><br />I despise Jason and Piper. I think they’re an Annabeth and Percy remake and I just didn’t like that in life and death situations the only person Piper cared about was Jason. It was annoying. However, finally, six books later I like them. Wow, that was hard to say. I think what I enjoyed the most was a) lack of Jason and b) Piper getting real about their relationship. Their relationship had been forged on lies – shout out to Hera, you bitch – and in such a high intense situation as war it is difficult to go back to normal life in which you can relax. I feel that this pair really showed the struggles of something like that and I am so happy Rick included it in the book.<br /><br />✗ GROVER IS BACK HAIL GROVER<br /><br />I said it earlier but Grover deserves more love. Grover goes out of his way to saves everyone’s butt and protect the world. I honestly can’t even express my excitement at getting his humour back in the books and seeing his dedication towards his friends, both old and new. He’s seriously Percy’s best friend and y’all sleep on him too much.<br /><br />✗THAT CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT ON APOLLO FINALLY STUCK<br /><br />I complained in my last review, The Dark Prophecy, about how Apollo took backward steps. Finally in The Burning Maze we see Apollo start thinking about others. He goes through so many emotions and has a general empathy that shocks even him. It was seriously enjoyable to see a god shocked at feeling something like empathy towards a mortal. I feel if Apollo had kept up with the same level of douchebaggery as the first book I would have had to put this book down but I was very pleasantly shocked by what Rick Riordan chose to do with this story.<br /><br />D I S L I K ES<br />✗ I DON’T HAVE ANY LMAO BYE<br /><br />I’m as shocked as you are. I don’t know what happened. I always have something I disliked about a book. I mean, The Burning Maze isn’t a perfect book either but I honestly just can’t pinpoint one thing I hated or that even irked me in this book. I had such a fun time reading it and I really can’t say anything negative. I’m speechless, for once. If you know me, you know this is a shock.<br /><br />Overall, The Burning Maze shocked me in the best way possible. I truly can’t put in words how much I did enjoy this book. I clearly tried and reading over this review made me cringe because I literally can’t express my enjoyment. I probably wouldn’t recommend this series to someone who hasn’t read Rick Riordan’s previous series, but if you want to give it a go I do still recommend it! The pacing was beautiful and the intensity of some of the characters emotions was intense. We finally got a sense of grief as well, that Rick has shied away from in previous books.<br /><br /><a>Also, if you're looking to buy any books over at Book Depository, feel free to use my affiliate link! I gain a small 5% commission at no extra cost to you.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8770837062207563705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616595698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11907647856594379353"><b>5</b>🌟<br/><br/>😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭...shit, i thought i was ready but i was <i>so</i> wrong<br/><br/><blockquote>

  <span id="freeText11907647856594379353" style="display:none"><b>5</b>🌟<br /><br />😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭😭...shit, i thought i was ready but i was <i>so</i> wrong<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>_____________________________</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Ok, I posted only crying emojis because I had many emotions but it was 3 am. Now, it's time for the <i>actual review</i> because I have some <i>thoughts</i>.<br /><br />Magnus Chase is still my favourite Rick Riordan's series, but <u>this is a close second</u> — I love the bad haikus. I love how annoying and yet still lovable Apollo can be. I love how casual LGBT rep is here. <br /><br />➽<b>This series has one of the greatest <u>character development</u></b><br /><br />I like how we started out with a really annoying Apollo in the book one. I instantly knew that there's so much potential with that and Uncle Rick did not disappoint. Apollo grows so much throughout the series and we're just at book 3 of 5. He still retains some of his annoying qualities but it only makes him much more interesting imo because it shows that by <u>becoming human he gained so much contrast</u>. He is scared shitless and the most defenseless of the group but he's ready to sacrifice himself. He didn't care about whole cities dying and he mourns someone he barely knew.<br /><br />➽<b>This is also a part of character development but I like how we see <u>both Meg and Apollo dealing with abuse in their lives</u> and <u>healing</u></b><br /><br />I like that <u>Apollo tries to help Meg</u> but he also knows when he needs to let her grow on her own. How he knows he can't force her to see things his way and that he respects her autonomy and supports her choices (unless they're really bad choices. Murder is <i>bad</i>, Meg.) How he realises similarities between his life and Meg's and how even he as a god had this experience. How that doesn't make either of them weak. How he helps her with misdirecting her anger...<br /><br />But also, I like how <u>Meg grows on her own</u>. How she goes back-and-forth and how realistic it is. How she gains her own support system and how that strengthens her. How she lets herself feel anger. How she lets herself feel happiness. How she slowly heals. <br /><br />➽<b>I love how Apollo being the god of <u>healing</u> and Demeter, Meg's mother, being the goddess of <u>growing</u> is exactly what both of them need</b><br /><br />➽<b>This book had a much darker feel to it than any of Riordan's books</b><br /><br />Usually I'm the first one to shout 'why do creators always insist on making all the bright and easy things darker and darker' but <u>it fits here</u>? There's still enough humour to counter it so it's not only all sad and serious but Apollo and Meg's arcs wouldn't work as well with the usual mood of Percy Jackson Verse. Here making things a bit darker has a function and it just works.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>__________________________<br /><br /> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/localbeehunters_nook/" rel="nofollow noopener">insta</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/localbeehunter" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> | <a href="https://localbeehuntersnook.home.blog/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> | <a href="https://booksirens.com/reviewer/9N1QFSM" rel="nofollow noopener">booksirens</a> | <a href="https://www.duolingo.com/localbeehunter" rel="nofollow noopener">duolingo</a></b>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2378332865" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2378332865" />
    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2378332865?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil (or bleed)" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed">Neil (or bleed)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2378332865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18120886890310768336">The Burning Maze is, by far, the best in this series, The Trials of Apollo. I don't know about you but I really did admire Apollo on this book. I mean, he's still the eccentric, conceited god but he continue to make progress as a god/mortal, emotionally and intellectually. He continue to realize the value of human and the human nature. And I just love how it was portrayed and delivered in the novel.<br/><br/>The Burning Maze is also the book, among the other Riordan's books that I felt the realness of the</span>
  <span id="freeText18120886890310768336" style="display:none">The Burning Maze is, by far, the best in this series, The Trials of Apollo. I don't know about you but I really did admire Apollo on this book. I mean, he's still the eccentric, conceited god but he continue to make progress as a god/mortal, emotionally and intellectually. He continue to realize the value of human and the human nature. And I just love how it was portrayed and delivered in the novel.<br /><br />The Burning Maze is also the book, among the other Riordan's books that I felt the realness of the characters and the events. (I mean I felt it too in his other books but this is the pinacle of realness, imo). All of it. I felt the punch of grief, the happiness, the excitement, the dread, everything. I am so entranced by this book. I am so hooked from the beginning until the end.<br /><br />Meg is also likable and adorable in this sequel. We've got to know more about her and her past. I dig back stories and character development that makes sense, thank you very much. Meg is badass, too. The kill kill kill attitude. Lol. Other characters are wonderful, too. Jason, Piper, GROVER, Coach Hedge, etc.<br /><br />Plotwise, I'm getting and digging it more and more. I still love the prophecy accompanied by the quest/ adventure of our dear demigods and god, for that matter. The humor is still gold, even it's subtle and self-deprecating. It still works for me.<br /><br />The Burning Maze is hell of a ride. I'm sure, this incoherent review of mine didn't really give justice on the beauty and greatness of this book but I knew you get the point.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18120886890310768336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2075923194" />
    <a title="Enne (they/he)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60021454-enne-they-he"><img alt="Enne (they/he)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577868041p2/60021454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2075923194?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Enne (they/he)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Enne (they/he)" href="/user/show/60021454-enne-they-he">Enne (they/he)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=z-2018-reads">z-2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=4-and-a-half-star">4-and-a-half-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=couldn-t-put-it-down">couldn-t-put-it-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=genre-urban-fantasy">genre-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=laugh-out-loud">laugh-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=good-action-sequences">good-action-sequences</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=pov-1st">pov-1st</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=anticipated-releases-2018">anticipated-releases-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60021454-enne-they-he?shelf=i-have-feelings">i-have-feelings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075923194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11814645696267578861"><blockquote>
  <i>”Remember what it’s like to be human.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars </b><br/><b>TW:</b> violence, death<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Writing</u>
</b><br/>It’s the classic Apollo-style writing that we had in the previous two Apollo books that I absolutely loved mixed with just classic Riordan writing that we get in all of his books and I also love. It’s funny, it’s got character, it’s easy to fly through. I appreciate it. There’s really not much else to be said about it.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Plot/Pacing</u>
</b><br/>It’s so fastpaced! Something is constantly happening and you can’t lose foc</span>
  <span id="freeText11814645696267578861" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>”Remember what it’s like to be human.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><b>4.5 stars </b><br /><b>TW:</b> violence, death<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Writing</u>
</b><br />It’s the classic Apollo-style writing that we had in the previous two Apollo books that I absolutely loved mixed with just classic Riordan writing that we get in all of his books and I also love. It’s funny, it’s got character, it’s easy to fly through. I appreciate it. There’s really not much else to be said about it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Plot/Pacing</u>
</b><br />It’s so fastpaced! Something is constantly happening and you can’t lose focus for even a second because if you do then you have to go back and reread paragraphs (which I did do, yes). There are so many new mythical creatures introduced in this book and the new emperor and ieterh it was just all really exciting in fastpaced and the Rick Riordan did that One Thing(TM) and broke all of our hearts. I will never forgive him for it. But, yes, plot was A+<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br />Apollo has developed and progressed so much a character starting from The Hidden Oracle that now he’s almost unrecognizable. Meg has, too. THE CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT WAS SO BEAUTIFULLY DONE AND I LOVE IT SO MUCH!!<br /><br />However, my favorite character still remains to be the Arrow of Dodona because, come on, Rick’s weapons are always his best characters.<br /><br />I also really enjoyed seeing all of the old characters that we got to see in this book and I loved seeing the new characters building relationships with the old characters and roerhioy hi I just really love Rick’s characters, I think we get the point, let’s move on now.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Overall</u>
</b><br />I LOVED THIS BOOK!! There is literally not a single thing I’d change about it except for maybe One Thing(tm), though I was pleasantly surprised by the fact that Rick would do something like One Thing(tm) and I think it’s good that he’s making those decisions. It raises the stakes, which is nice to see.<br /><br />~~~<br />Why do you do this to me, Rick? Why??? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11814645696267578861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1559334294" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559334294" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1559334294?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=award-goodreads-choice">award-goodreads-choice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-comedy">genre-comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-middle-grade">bage-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=sub-flying">sub-flying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-coming-of-age">genre-coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series-unfinished">series-unfinished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=sub-overcoming-adversity">sub-overcoming-adversity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1559334294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5394542939960532713">I am a Rick fan. His books are so fun. Of all the series I have read, this is my least favorite series and I've been trying to figure out why. It has Rick's crisp wit and humor that the rest have. His characters are interesting and we are invested in them. Something is just a little bit off with this one. I do enjoy it, but I'm comparing this to all the other Rick books.<br/><br/>I think this book series has more of a melancholy tone. I think Apollo brings a bit of sadness to the story. He has so much to </span>
  <span id="freeText5394542939960532713" style="display:none">I am a Rick fan. His books are so fun. Of all the series I have read, this is my least favorite series and I've been trying to figure out why. It has Rick's crisp wit and humor that the rest have. His characters are interesting and we are invested in them. Something is just a little bit off with this one. I do enjoy it, but I'm comparing this to all the other Rick books.<br /><br />I think this book series has more of a melancholy tone. I think Apollo brings a bit of sadness to the story. He has so much to compare. The thing is, I love the fact that Apollo is human and the story revolves around that. It's a brilliant concept and I do enjoy that, but he has an ennui about him. I do hope that once he is a god again, that we get to meet him again in a future quest and he will talk and remember his time as a human, but we know he won't. He's been human several times and once he's a god he forgets the humanity he had.<br /><br />Usually, we know that this is a safe story, but Rick breaks that rule her in this story and it's very emotional. I was moved by what happened.<br /><br />This should be a great story, but for some reason, of the 3 books in this series, this is my least favorite book. I don't exactly know why accept the above. <br /><br />They are having to go back into the maze to defeat Medusa. A few of our previous heroes do show up in this book to help out the quest. <br /><br />I just love the relationship between Meg and Apollo. It's so wonderful. Rick has such a gift with characters. Meg is growing as a character and it's a great thing to watch. I still like this series and I do look forward to where the story goes and how it concludes. I have hope it can pick up and end on a high note. I will say that I haven't read any stories of Apollo's time on Earth, so I have no idea where Rick is going with the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5394542939960532713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2091527602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091527602" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2091527602?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36544788-the-burning-maze">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091527602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14088505552986552239">The third instalment in The Trials of Apollo series by Rick Riordan sees our heroes face the final Roman emperor in the Triumvirate, as well as meeting a large number of dryads in a very hot and desert like California. We’re also joined by Piper and Jason, demigod heroes last seen in The Heroes of Olympus series - and let’s just say they’re on rather fractious terms...<br/><br/>This picks up the action straight away, as we see Apollo, Meg and Grover running for their lives in the Labyrinth while pursed by</span>
  <span id="freeText14088505552986552239" style="display:none">The third instalment in The Trials of Apollo series by Rick Riordan sees our heroes face the final Roman emperor in the Triumvirate, as well as meeting a large number of dryads in a very hot and desert like California. We’re also joined by Piper and Jason, demigod heroes last seen in The Heroes of Olympus series - and let’s just say they’re on rather fractious terms...<br /><br />This picks up the action straight away, as we see Apollo, Meg and Grover running for their lives in the Labyrinth while pursed by blood thirsty owls. As usual, there’s a big dollop of humour, mythology and action here - but I also found this a bit darker than the previous instalments. In suddenly feels as though the gang are really at risk of loosing everything, without any help from former allies or Godly powers to save them this time. There’s an overall feeling of anticipation and dread that runs throughout, which I actually found more exciting. <br /><br />As usual, there’s an eclectic mix of supporting characters. I was particularly drawn to the various desert dryads, such as Prickly Pear and Aloe Vera who seemed to perfectly incorporate their plants nature into their personality. I also liked seeing the development in Apollo, embracing his human nature more (whether he wants to or not) and accepting responsibility for his actions. However, I do miss a little of the old Apollo arrogance and swagger. I hope that hadn’t been lost forever. <br /><br />The antagonist here is also a lot more intimidating compared to Commodus and Nero. When we finally meet him, he seems to exude an aura of menace and madness that’s unhinged and unpredictable. I’m looking forward to seeing what he brings in the next instalment. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[My only let down was Jason’s death. It felt rather flippant and gratuitous rather than furthering the plot in anyway. I was actually more upset by Money Maker’s death, which managed to be both horrific and touching. I’m hoping that by returning his body to Camp Jupiter, his death will be more fulfilling in the next book, as he’s given a proper Roman burial and his friends will have a chance to grieve. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="14088505552986552239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14642616767847194207">Darn you uncle rick. WHY CANT YOU WRITE FASTER!!<br/>Update: THE COVER!   <span id="freeText14642616767847194207" style="display:none">Darn you uncle rick. WHY CANT YOU WRITE FASTER!!<br />Update: THE COVER! This book was awesome! The third book is always a turning point in Rick Riordan's five part series. This book was no different. It was happy at some points and sad in others. I am so glad Grover has made come back. Plus we see an appearance from Piper and Jason. Many people are not fans of them, but personally I loved those characters and I still do. Rick Riordan did take some risks with those characters and I feel like those things were necessary, although they did hurt my heart. There was so much character development in this novel. Apollo became more caring and compassionate. Meg opened up a bit. Grover showed soooooo much bravery and Piper realized something important in her relationship with Jason.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4052903528024305001">So I really loved this. Apollo is definitely my favorite god [in the general Riordanverse], Meg is great, and it's nice to see some cameos from familiar characters throughout [although I still cannot believe that <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Rick just killed off Jason like that???   <span id="freeText4052903528024305001" style="display:none">So I really loved this. Apollo is definitely my favorite god [in the general Riordanverse], Meg is great, and it's nice to see some cameos from familiar characters throughout [although I still cannot believe that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rick just killed off Jason like that??? It feels wrong for him to die outside of his own series lol Like if Batman just died in some random Aquaman issue and never came back, because I'm pretty sure he won't be bringing him back to life but I guess we'll see <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>]. But this is the middle book of five and it definitely felt the plot was dragging a bit in places or that we were just moving from point A to point B to get ready for the next book. Middle Book Syndrome comes for us all but it was still a really fun time overall. I would read a million of these books so I'm happy he keeps writing them lol</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YmhP94HWm8N81smrTbRpmgg+SK2kJuw5ZuxSZW62PxqcrVcch9bKhBPnAyg0qSFoGUWhSdy8HlqJnnC8N7PAWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nMXK9elEucKpWMgSZ/ac3EPpcvFkVYsF/lcJWUPut11iANIe70TohcZpApEe69QuUpKbFRzPeWYRJSuAGutIHA==')})
  }

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_36222611'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36222611-aru-shah-and-the-end-of-time?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Aru Shah and the End of Time (Pandava Quartet, #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/13695109.Roshani_Chokshi?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Roshani Chokshi<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.09 avg rating &mdash; 13,692 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2018\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer13990764788823716956\">Twelve-year-old Aru Shah has a tendency to stretch the truth in order to fit in at school. While her classmates are jetting off to family vacations in exotic locales, she\'ll be spending her autumn break at home, in the Museum of Ancient Indian Art an<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13990764788823716956\" style=\"display:none\">Twelve-year-old Aru Shah has a tendency to stretch the truth in order to fit in at school. While her classmates are jetting off to family vacations in exotic locales, she\'ll be spending her autumn break at home, in the Museum of Ancient Indian Art and Culture, waiting for her mom to return from her latest archeological trip. Is it any wonder that Aru makes up stories about being royalty, traveling to Paris, and having a chauffeur?\n\nOne day, three schoolmates show up at Aru\'s doorstep to catch her in a lie. They don\'t believe her claim that the museum\'s Lamp of Bharata is cursed, and they dare Aru to prove it. Just a quick light, Aru thinks. Then she can get herself out of this mess and never ever fib again.\n\nBut lighting the lamp has dire consequences.
